  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_78ad75be-2bc0-45c0-94ec-5bad4b6c42bb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_156637799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156637799" />
    <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten"><img alt="Jeffrey Keeten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301087352p2/3427339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156637799?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeffrey Keeten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeffrey Keeten" href="/user/show/3427339-jeffrey-keeten">Jeffrey Keeten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/22087188-the-thin-man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=book-to-film">book-to-film</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=hollywood">hollywood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3427339-jeffrey-keeten?shelf=hardboiled">hardboiled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156637799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer725626825753207753"><b>We found a table. Nora said: "She's pretty."<br/><br/>"If you like them like that."<br/><br/>She grinned at me. "You got types?"<br/><br/>"Only you, darling - lanky brunettes with wicked jaws."<br/><br/>"And how about the red-head you wandered off with at Quinns' last night?"<br/><br/>"That's silly," I said. "She just wanted to show me some French etchings.”</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Nick20and20Nora20Charles_zpsfferepr0.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535791735i/26233994.jpg' alt=' photo Nick20and20Nora20Charles_zpsfferepr0.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>It is almost impossible for me to separate the book from the movies. When I decided to reread this classic that spawned six great movies, Nick Charles was of course William Powell, and N</span>
  <span id="freeText725626825753207753" style="display:none"><b>We found a table. Nora said: "She's pretty."<br><br>"If you like them like that."<br><br>She grinned at me. "You got types?"<br><br>"Only you, darling - lanky brunettes with wicked jaws."<br><br>"And how about the red-head you wandered off with at Quinns' last night?"<br><br>"That's silly," I said. "She just wanted to show me some French etchings.”</b><br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/Nick20and20Nora20Charles_zpsfferepr0.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535791735i/26233994.jpg" alt=" photo Nick20and20Nora20Charles_zpsfferepr0.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It is almost impossible for me to separate the book from the movies. When I decided to reread this classic that spawned six great movies, Nick Charles was of course William Powell, and Nora Charles was of course Myrna Loy. Those actors are forever Nick and Nora for me. The book is famous for the witty exchanges between Nora and Nick, but the book is somewhat overshadowed by the wonderful repartee between Powell and Loy over the course of the six movies. The scintillating, amusing conversations are punctuated by Loy’s uptilted nose and impish smile and Powell’s infectious grin as he takes pleasure in toying with his wife’s state of mind. <br><br>We must not forget the Charles’s dog Asta. <i>”That afternoon I took Asta for a walk, explained to two people that she was a Schnauzer and not a cross between a Scottie and an Irish terrier….”</i> The dog, Skippy, who was cast in the movie was a Wire Fox Terrier. I have a six month old Scottish Terrier, whose name is Astra after the state motto of Kansas, ad astra per aspera. Astra in Latin means stars. For those who know us and how much we love <i>The Thin Man</i> movies, they always assume that it is also a nod to Asta...and they would be right. Asta doesn’t provide the comic relief in the book that he does in the movie, but he is a presence for most of the book. There are usually some light hearted moments with Asta in every movie where they are chasing him around the room trying to retrieve a vital clue from between his jaws or other scenes where he is just doing something terminally adorable that brings a bit more lightheartedness to the script. <br><br>Dashiell Hammett based the Charles’s off his own tempestuous on-again and off-again relationship with Lillian Hellman. From what I’ve read, he definitely must have focused on the sunnier side of the relationship because one of the most enjoyable things about this dynamic couple is their friendly, jocular interactions, highlighted with the rich overtones of how much they admire and like one another. Hellman and Hammett fought like Siamese Fighting Fish. The fights that Nick and Nora get into are playful, funny, and foreplay that provides Nick with an opportunity to grab Nora and plant a kiss on her that will shake her fillings. <br><br>There really aren’t a lot of happy married couples in noir literature. Hardboiled mystery writers seem to focus on characters as singular individuals. They are usually divorced or single, and if they are married, they certainly aren’t happily married. Nick and Nora are best together, and as the investigation in the story moves forward, they seem a bit unmoored when they are apart. They drink heavily, mirroring the Hellman and Hammett relationship in that aspect. <br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/06db8479-c5f5-41a8-8075-5a91afd938be_zpsx8ae7y5u.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535791735i/26233993.png" alt=" photo 06db8479-c5f5-41a8-8075-5a91afd938be_zpsx8ae7y5u.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>”She sat on the sofa beside me. ‘Now out with it. If you skip a single word, I’ll---’<br><br>‘I’d have to have a drink before I could do any talking.’<br><br>She cursed me and brought me a drink.”</i><br><br>Nick doesn’t want to investigate crime. He is perfectly happy spending his days drinking martinis and looking after Nora’s money, but Nora is obsessed with his previous life as a private investigator and certainly has a rosy, unrealistic view of the profession. So the way the stories go in the book and the movies is that invariably Nora drags Nick into an investigation. He reluctantly agrees to see what he can do, which is to cleverly solve the crime and wrap up the criminals for the bungling cops to haul off to jail. In this book, he is investigating the murder of a mistress of the mad scientist Clyde Wynant, and in the course of his investigation, he and Nora have to contend with the whole Wynant clan, each as loony as the next. The ex-wife Mimi is a real piece of work, a combination of curves and cunning. She tries to use both assets on Nick, and needless to say, things get out of hand. <br><br><i>”’Tell me something, Nick. Tell me the truth: when you were wrestling with Mimi, didn’t you have an erection?’<br><br>‘Oh, a little.’<br><br>She laughed and got up from the floor. ‘If you aren’t a disgusting old lecher,’ she said.”</i><br><br>Did she just say erection? My, my goodness sakes, Nora. Do you kiss Nick with that mouth? Why yes, she does. <br><br><a href="https://s1183.photobucket.com/user/jkeeten/media/thinmankiss_zpscqrjijie.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1535791735i/26233992.jpg" alt=" photo thinmankiss_zpscqrjijie.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If you take a drink every time Nick orders an alcoholic beverage, you will be plowed by the time you get 30 pages into the book or thirty minutes into the movie. The heavy drinking in this book and the movies might be more than a hint to Dashiell Hammett’s own struggle with alcohol. It might also be the key to why he stuck with Hellman so long. She was a heavy drinker too, and as happens sometimes, couples bond over drinking. Their drinking escalates with dual encouragement, and they become caught in a cycle of maladaptive drinking. I certainly can feel jealous of Nick and Nora’s lifestyle. They can leave a city at the drop of the hat and go to any other city in the world. Money is not an issue, and time is something they have in abundance. They are about as free as two people can ever hope to be. Oh, and they are hopelessly, head over heels in love with one another. Freedom, plenty of money, and someone who loves us, what more could anyone wish for? I highly recommend the book and the movies paired with a few vodka martinis shaken not stirred. <br><br>If you wish to see more of my most recent book and movie reviews, visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeffreykeeten.com">http://www.jeffreykeeten.com</a><br>I also have a Facebook blogger page at:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten">https://www.facebook.com/JeffreyKeeten</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="725626825753207753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_26108453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26108453" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26108453?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780394717746" href="/book/show/1347301.The_Thin_Man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=whodunit">whodunit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2015-reread">2015-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=detectives">detectives</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26108453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10449516536372067528">I invented a new drinking game based on <i>The Thin Man</i> and tried to give it a test run when I re-read it. The rules were simple, every time that main character Nick Charles took a drink, I’d take one, too. However, I had to be taken to the hospital for treatment of extreme alcohol poisoning by the second chapter. So don’t try that.<br/><br/>Nick used to be a private detective in New York, but he left that behind when he married Nora and moved to California to take over the management of the various business</span>
  <span id="freeText10449516536372067528" style="display:none">I invented a new drinking game based on <i>The Thin Man</i> and tried to give it a test run when I re-read it. The rules were simple, every time that main character Nick Charles took a drink, I’d take one, too. However, I had to be taken to the hospital for treatment of extreme alcohol poisoning by the second chapter. So don’t try that.<br /><br />Nick used to be a private detective in New York, but he left that behind when he married Nora and moved to California to take over the management of the various businesses her father left her. Why couldn’t Nora run them herself? Because this was 1933 so in addition to casual alcoholism being an accepted part of everyday life, the lady folks weren’t going to be left in charge of something as important as business. Ah, the good ole days…<br /><br />Nick and Nora are on a Christmas vacation trip back to New York when Nick bumps into the daughter of an old client of his, Clyde Wynatt. Wynatt has gone missing and a woman associated him was murdered so everyone from the family to Wynatt’s lawyer to the cops think that Nick is working the case. Nick would prefer to just do some more drinking, but Nora is intrigued by the idea of watching her husband play detective and other events transpire to pull Nick into reluctantly investigating in between glasses of whiskey.<br /><br />Hammett’s <i>The Maltese Falcon</i> and <i>Red Harvest</i> are two of my favorite detective novels as well as being considered classics of the genre. This one shows off a bit of his versatility in that it reads as a witty comedy with a dash of murder rather than a hard boiled mystery. The banter between Nick and Nora is fun, and his casual remarks about needing a drink with breakfast just to “cut the phlegm” make for their own kind of anachronistic amusement. <br /><br />The mystery is kind of a convoluted mess, but Hammett managed to tie it all together with a resolution that makes sense. It’s not my favorite book of his, but it’s got a dated charm that makes it a fun read. 3.65 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10449516536372067528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1157179930" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1157179930?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157179930" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5200049884273260174">I <i>really</i> wasn't expecting to love this one as much as I did.<br/>I just wanted to read it because it seems to be one of the gold standards for hardboiled detective stories. But I didn't think I'd actually <i>like</i> the characters.<br/>They were so cool, though! <br/>And now all I want is to have a drink (or ten) with Nick & Nora Charles.<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603897991ra/30300800.gif' width='400' height='260' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There's really nothing like a couple of lovable drinkers reluctantly solving a dangerous mystery. The story <i>could have</i> been dark and depressing what with all the lies, beatings, bi</span>
  <span id="freeText5200049884273260174" style="display:none">I <i>really</i> wasn't expecting to love this one as much as I did.<br>I just wanted to read it because it seems to be one of the gold standards for hardboiled detective stories. But I didn't think I'd actually <i>like</i> the characters.<br>They were so cool, though! <br>And now all I want is to have a drink (or ten) with Nick &amp; Nora Charles.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603897991ra/30300800.gif" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's really nothing like a couple of lovable drinkers reluctantly solving a dangerous mystery. The story <i>could have</i> been dark and depressing what with all the lies, beatings, bigamy, adultery, and murder. But it never felt like anything but a fun romp through the seedy underworld.<br>The dialogue is really what makes it here. It's snappy, and quirky, and witty, and just plain fun.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603897691ra/30300754.gif" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Plus, it's short! <br>The length was perfect for someone with my attention span (&lt;--that of a squirrel), so if you're one of those people who aren't <i>quite</i> sure you want to read something written in 1934, it might make you feel better to know it's only a couple hundred pages.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603901665ra/30301177.gif" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok. So here's how much I loved this one: As soon as I was done, I immediately downloaded <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29999.The_Maltese_Falcon" title="The Maltese Falcon by Dashiell Hammett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Maltese Falcon</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30007.The_Glass_Key" title="The Glass Key by Dashiell Hammett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glass Key</a>. And now I've got to find all the Nick &amp; Nora movies...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603901665ra/30301178.gif" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Highly Recommended!</b></span>

<div id="review_3440749098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3440749098" />
    <a title="David Putnam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam"><img alt="David Putnam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372638034p2/5463364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3440749098?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Putnam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Putnam" href="/user/show/5463364-david-putnam">David Putnam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3440749098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14332309299800520778">I enjoyed this book a great deal. For years I have heard readers and literary pundits talk about how Chandler and Hammett are the grandfathers of mystery. For me, Chandler has always been the pinnacle, and no one else comes close. His turn of phrase and perception of life is unmatched. I read Hammett’s Red Harvest and thought, “eh.” Red Harvest was an okay book but not in the same league as Chandler. With, The Thin Man Hammett uses a different style than Red Harvest. His prose is more economic, </span>
  <span id="freeText14332309299800520778" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book a great deal. For years I have heard readers and literary pundits talk about how Chandler and Hammett are the grandfathers of mystery. For me, Chandler has always been the pinnacle, and no one else comes close. His turn of phrase and perception of life is unmatched. I read Hammett’s Red Harvest and thought, “eh.” Red Harvest was an okay book but not in the same league as Chandler. With, The Thin Man Hammett uses a different style than Red Harvest. His prose is more economic, and he does a great job displaying character through dialogue which is what I prefer. This book runs very quickly and reminded me so much of the movie, I couldn’t help but hear and see William Powell and Myrna Loy while reading this book. Hammett moved way up on my list and I intend on reading all the Thin Man series and sample other Hammett books.<br />David Putnam author of The Bruno Johnson Series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14332309299800520778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3079158784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3079158784" />
    <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton"><img alt="J.L.   Sutton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438142892p2/3675162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3079158784?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.L.   Sutton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.L.   Sutton" href="/user/show/3675162-j-l-sutton">J.L.   Sutton</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer7711706276588920504"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576083756i/28595599._SX540_.jpg' alt='Image result for the thin man quotes' width='400' height='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In Dashiell Hammett's The Thin Man, the relationship of Nick Charles and his wife Nora makes this stand out from other traditional noire-detective novels. While Nick has many of the same Sam Spadish qualities as other detectives in the genre, he actually listens to and values the opinion of his wife (even if his language is sometimes patronizing). Their banter also shows the tough guy personae on display when he interrogates suspects is not how he really lives, but how he does his job. I'm not c</span>
  <span id="freeText7711706276588920504" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576083756i/28595599._SX540_.jpg" alt="Image result for the thin man quotes" width="400" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In Dashiell Hammett's The Thin Man, the relationship of Nick Charles and his wife Nora makes this stand out from other traditional noire-detective novels. While Nick has many of the same Sam Spadish qualities as other detectives in the genre, he actually listens to and values the opinion of his wife (even if his language is sometimes patronizing). Their banter also shows the tough guy personae on display when he interrogates suspects is not how he really lives, but how he does his job. I'm not claiming this is groundbreaking, but it is still refreshing in this genre. <br><br>Overall, I enjoyed the read! As an aside: I would like to be able to get as much done as Nick Charles does after so many drinks! I'm not sure I would even be able to find my way home! 3.5 stars</span>

<div id="review_387786777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/387786777" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/387786777?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer387786777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2149924608599339487">Nick Charles used to work in a private detective agency, got married later, came into good money, and took on a hard and thankless job of managing his investments. The beginning of the book finds Nick and his wife Nora in New York. It seemed they were drinking happily (and heavily) in a bar. Later it turned out it was just a mild warm-up routine for some very serious alcohol consumption. We just woke up - let's have a drink. Having trouble sleeping - double scotch is in order. A guest came - dri</span>
  <span id="freeText2149924608599339487" style="display:none">Nick Charles used to work in a private detective agency, got married later, came into good money, and took on a hard and thankless job of managing his investments. The beginning of the book finds Nick and his wife Nora in New York. It seemed they were drinking happily (and heavily) in a bar. Later it turned out it was just a mild warm-up routine for some very serious alcohol consumption. We just woke up - let's have a drink. Having trouble sleeping - double scotch is in order. A guest came - drinks for everybody! A guest just finished his drink - better finish mine and have another one. Coming back from visiting a toilet - celebration time! <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547862395i/26938938.jpg" alt="Drunk" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you are waiting for me to start giving an outline of a plot - this is exactly what I do. The book convinced me being rich is boring. All you do is inviting guests to your place - the same people, mind you. Being rich is also really bad for one's health and hopes of long life as no human liver can withstand this tsunami of strong alcohol consumed by Nick (with occasional help from Nora).<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547862616i/26938947._SX540_.jpg" alt="Alcohol" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Drink as he might Nick still ended up being mixed up in a murder case. A secretary of an inventor he used to know was killed with inventor himself completely disappearing from the face of the Earth. For some reason everybody and their brother decided Nick is the one to solve the mystery. Nick certainly did not think so, but after being shot at he decided to nudge the police into more thoughtful investigation. Between his drinks, obviously. <br><br>People say in the classic movie based on this book the chemistry between the actors playing Nick and Nora totally carried it. In the book however the chemistry is quite weak. To be fair I found the ex-wife of disappeared inventor and their children to be something out of this world - all of them. The rest of the characters served their roles, but were nothing to write home about. <br><br>The book changed my views. I used to think there are only two phases in lives of drunkards: <br>1. Being drunk.<br>2. Suffering from a hangover. <br>Nick managed to be perpetually stuck in phase 1. I have not realized it was psychically possible. Surely this is when pink elephants pay you a visit?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547862887i/26938956.png" alt="Pink elephant" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Real Life™ full of great irony. Take my case: less than a month ago I stated that I have yet to see a boring book written by Dashiell Hammett. Now I have to eat my words as this one while not exactly boring, but at least the weakest story from the father of noir mystery. So the rating is 3 stars and now my life has a purpose: I need to see the movie. Let us drink to this!!! Cheers!!!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547862485i/26938939._SX540_.jpg" alt="Cheers" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>Oops, I think I caught something from Nick!!! Quickly, somebody call AA and book me an appointment for their next meeting!</b>
</i></span>

<div id="review_403417989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/403417989" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/403417989?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=mystery-detective-thriller">mystery-detective-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer403417989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9288749194039950654">The Thin Man is a (sort of) noir novel by one of the greats of noir crime history, Dashiell Hammett, who is best known for creating Sam Spade in The Maltese Falcon. But The Thin Man was also a well known and much read series, and maybe still is. This one features the lush drinking duo Nick and Nora Charles and opens very much like a screwball comedy. The movie version is a classic, and maybe better than the book in some ways. <br/><br/>“Nora: "How do you feel?" <br/>Nick: "Terrible. I must've gone to bed sober</span>
  <span id="freeText9288749194039950654" style="display:none">The Thin Man is a (sort of) noir novel by one of the greats of noir crime history, Dashiell Hammett, who is best known for creating Sam Spade in The Maltese Falcon. But The Thin Man was also a well known and much read series, and maybe still is. This one features the lush drinking duo Nick and Nora Charles and opens very much like a screwball comedy. The movie version is a classic, and maybe better than the book in some ways. <br /><br />“Nora: "How do you feel?" <br />Nick: "Terrible. I must've gone to bed sober.” <br /><br />Hammett is most famous for being just so damned clever, and especially with dialogue. He keeps the jokes coming, and it is entertaining. Now if you like your noir truly scary and brutal, read Jim Thompson or Richard Stark’s Parker series. No laughs, but lots of terrific writing. And better stories. This one is light-hearted, and he doesn’t really care much about the story, so I am not even going to talk much about it. The novel could be plotted in this way: <br /><br />Part One: Nick and Nora drink heavily and tell jokes about how Nick got out of the detective business to marry rich Nora, and so on.<br /><br />Part two: They solve a crime featuring the dizzy blond (are there ever dizzy brunettes? Sure, but the blonds are the ones that have the most fun, apparently). She sets the standard for a beautiful babe who is a chronic liar throughout. I already can hardly remember what happens or how they solve it, but there is some brutality, since it is noir, but <br /><br />Part Three: Nick and Nora begin drinking “like a fish,” as they say, again.<br /><br />Reminded me of the days when loveable drunks were a regular feature in literature and tv such as Crazy Guggenheim on Red Skelton:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1ic5vMbXQvU">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1ic5v...</a><br /><br />Or Dudley Moore in 10:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9qHA9iDmxl4&amp;frags=pl%2Cwn">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=9qHA9...</a><br /><br />Finally: Hammett is a terrific writer of dialogue.<br /><br />A clip from the movie, which I recommend to read after the book.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bSThEEeFYeU">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bSThE...</a><br /><br />4.5 stars. 5 for creating the screwball detective duo Nick and Nora and the goofy girl and the dialogue and 2 stars for the story, which is sort of not what Hammett seemed to care about here. Ah, give me a drink, I had fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9288749194039950654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_623041224" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623041224" />
    <a title="Dan Schwent" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent"><img alt="Dan Schwent" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593973948p2/870755.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623041224?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Schwent" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Schwent" href="/user/show/870755-dan-schwent">Dan Schwent</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780394717746" href="/book/show/1347301.The_Thin_Man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=crime-and-mystery">crime-and-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623041224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1066084669350246888">An inventor goes missing and his mistress winds up dead. Former detective Nick Charles wants nothing to do with the case but keeps getting drawn in. With his plucky wife Nora, can Nick get things sorted out so he can get back to his drinking?<br/><br/>The Thin Man was not at all like I expected. After reading the exploits of Sam Spade and the Continental Op, I expected more of the same. The Thin Man is much more humorous than Hammett's earlier works and I found myself liking it quite a bit.<br/><br/>Nick Charles, f</span>
  <span id="freeText1066084669350246888" style="display:none">An inventor goes missing and his mistress winds up dead. Former detective Nick Charles wants nothing to do with the case but keeps getting drawn in. With his plucky wife Nora, can Nick get things sorted out so he can get back to his drinking?<br /><br />The Thin Man was not at all like I expected. After reading the exploits of Sam Spade and the Continental Op, I expected more of the same. The Thin Man is much more humorous than Hammett's earlier works and I found myself liking it quite a bit.<br /><br />Nick Charles, former detective, is quite a character. He's smart, sharp witted, and he likes the sauce. He's such a raging alcoholic that Matthew Scudder and Nick Stefanos once staged an intervention for him BEFORE they got off the sauce. "Nick, we like week-long benders as much as the next guy but you might have a problem..." <br /><br />His wife, Nora, sticks by her man, even if he probably smells like a distillery most of the time due to all the alcohol he consumes. The one-liners each of them fire off are infinitely more interesting than the plot. I'm pretty sure the plot is only here for Nick and Nora to bounce lines around and give them something to do between drinks.<br /><br />The writing is top notch for the era as well. As always, once I forgave Hammett for not being Raymond Chandler, it was off to the races. Quotable lines abound:<br />“Nora: "How do you feel?" <br />Nick: "Terrible. I must've gone to bed sober.” <br /><br />“Nick: "Don't you think maybe a drink would help you to sleep?"<br />Nora: "No, thanks."<br />Nick: "Maybe it would if I took one.” <br /><br />The plot was suitably serpentine and the interplay between Nick and Nora kept me engaged throughout. The rapid-fire dialogue was by far my favorite part of the book. Didn't Nick and Nora's dynamic in The Thin Man inspire J.D. Robb's In Death series? It's a shame Hammett didn't write more Nick and Nora books. Four stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1066084669350246888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_588182392" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/588182392" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/588182392?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer588182392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6007378437521729740">"We didn't come to New York to stay sober."<br/><br/><i>The Thin Man</i> is best read with a drink in hand. Do you have a drink? Do you need a refresher? Would you like another? Above all else, it is important that you be drinking!<br/><br/>Seriously...DRINK! <br/><br/>My god, a lot of alcohol is consumed in this book! It reads as if Ernest Hemingway had taken up crime noir. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617801.jpg' width='133' height='120' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617802._SX540_.jpg' width='133' height='120' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617803._SX540_.jpg' width='133' height='120' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In <i>The Thin Man</i>, Nick Charles, private detective, has hung up his hat. Nora, his wife, kinda wishes he hadn't. She likes wrapping her head around a good myster</span>
  <span id="freeText6007378437521729740" style="display:none">"We didn't come to New York to stay sober."<br><br><i>The Thin Man</i> is best read with a drink in hand. Do you have a drink? Do you need a refresher? Would you like another? Above all else, it is important that you be drinking!<br><br>Seriously...DRINK! <br><br>My god, a lot of alcohol is consumed in this book! It reads as if Ernest Hemingway had taken up crime noir. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617801.jpg" width="133" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617802._SX540_.jpg" width="133" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414170211i/11617803._SX540_.jpg" width="133" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In <i>The Thin Man</i>, Nick Charles, private detective, has hung up his hat. Nora, his wife, kinda wishes he hadn't. She likes wrapping her head around a good mystery. Well, a good one comes along in the form of murder for money, and Charles' old friends are all wrapped up in it. <br><br>The plot unfolds essentially in three places: at the Charles', at their friends', and at a speakeasy...each place being as well stocked with liquor as the next. Other than drinking, they don't do much of anything. And they don't really go anywhere, unless it's someplace to drink. They hang around and tie one on while they try to figure out whodunnit. <br><br>The writing is solid, the plot feels sound, the characters are a little dramatic (don't get me started on the women...<i>these dames is batty!</i>), but once all that's in motion, the book as a whole feels static. And then Hammett pulled a Melville...<br><br>At least Herman Melville was writing a novel about whales when he inserted that non-fiction book-sized treatise on the whale species. Yes, it took the reader right out of the story for a damn long time, but subjects were related. Hammett goes into great detail in a long passage on the Packer cannibal case of 1873-74. Was it necessary? Intrinsic to the plot? Or was it tossed in for its shock value? A bit of sensationalism to spice up a book that was getting a tad boring? Either way, the aside is overlong by a LONG SHOT.<br><br>Dashiell Hammett, author of <i>The Maltese Falcon</i> pretty much invented this genre, so perhaps I should lay off. But I'm not always one to treat revered things precious-like...just the stuff that's precious to me...so I'm docking this a star for Hammett's ol' slight of hand writer's trick. Otherwise it's not a bad little book. <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6007378437521729740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144601685" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144601685" />
    <a title="Grace Tjan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1889855-grace-tjan"><img alt="Grace Tjan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307595874p2/1889855.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144601685?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace Tjan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace Tjan" href="/user/show/1889855-grace-tjan">Grace Tjan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1889855-grace-tjan?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1889855-grace-tjan?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1889855-grace-tjan?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1889855-grace-tjan?shelf=hardboiled">hardboiled</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144601685" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10932267735849786141">What I learned from this book (in no particular order):<br/><br/>1.	A speakeasy is <i>the</i> proper place for a man to wait for his wife to finish her shopping.<br/><br/>2.	A Schnauzer is NOT a cross between a Scottie and an Irish terrier.<br/><br/>3.	“I hit Nora with my left hand, knocking her down across the room.” If a bad guy points a gun at you and your wife, the standard operating procedure is to knock her out to prevent her from becoming hysterical over such a potentially distressing situation. <br/><br/>4.	Women do not really mind b</span>
  <span id="freeText10932267735849786141" style="display:none">What I learned from this book (in no particular order):<br /><br />1.	A speakeasy is <i>the</i> proper place for a man to wait for his wife to finish her shopping.<br /><br />2.	A Schnauzer is NOT a cross between a Scottie and an Irish terrier.<br /><br />3.	“I hit Nora with my left hand, knocking her down across the room.” If a bad guy points a gun at you and your wife, the standard operating procedure is to knock her out to prevent her from becoming hysterical over such a potentially distressing situation. <br /><br />4.	Women do not really mind being knocked out for such reasons by their loving spouses. She would mildly protest, but would quickly forget it over a few drinks.<br /><br />5.	“Feminine brain-storms” cause hysteria in women. Italians and other foreigners are also prone to hysterics.<br /><br />6.	A Scotch and soda is a panacea for insomnia, and taken first thing in the morning before breakfast, would keep you awake during the day. Having up to 5 or 6 drinks a day would not keep you from being a brilliant dick.<br /><br />7.	Policemen’s liquor is no good. Never partake of any, even though it’s terribly tempting.<br /><br />8.	A dame “with hair on her chest” is admirable. <br /><br />9.	Women’s intuition is not to be belittled, even though they are prone to hysterics.<br /><br />10.	 Flirtatious banter, directed at any receptive female, would get a man out of any number of tight situations. <br /><br /><br /><b>Other Random Observations</b><br /><br /><br />Number of dead bodies: 3 <br /><br />Number of alcoholic drink consumed by the protagonist: 21<br /><br />Number of cute canine interludes: 8<br /><br />Number of un-PC racial epithet: 1<br /><br />Number of incident of spousal abuse by the protagonist: 1<br /><br /><br />BUT SERIOUSLY,<br /><br />I expected this to be a shining example of the 1930’s noir/screwball comedy, starring an amusing, bantering couple, hard-drinkin’ tough guys and smoky-eyed femme fatales. It certainly delivers some of these elements in generous portions. However, the banter is only mildly amusing, and the twist ending is achieved through the concealment of certain crucial facts from the reader --- not my preferred kind of mystery writing. There is some social commentary, although nothing overt, considering that Hammett was a Communist; and a perfectly adequate, if rather bland, description of the seedier underbelly of Prohibition era New York City. Raymond Chandler, with his vivid similes, deliciously quotable dialogue and atmospheric evocation of LA seems to be the superior noir writer.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10932267735849786141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_789311885" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789311885" />
    <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan"><img alt="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553101944p2/4728718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/789311885?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Algernon (Darth Anyan)" href="/user/show/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan">Algernon (Darth Anyan)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4728718-algernon-darth-anyan?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer789311885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198668124397173418"><br/>This Christmas you are invited to a party of hard liquor, witty repartee and murder in the company of Nick and Nora Charles. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387799589i/7673286.jpg' alt='Powell & Loy' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A hardboiled crime comedy might seem like an oddball choice for a winter holiday read, but Dashiell Hammett manages to mix together not only killer martinis, but also a succesful marriage between the mean and dirty Prohibition Era gumshoe detective and the British slick and sophisticated whodunits of Agatha Christie or Dorothy Sayers. Spiced up with some of that enchanting</span>
  <span id="freeText16198668124397173418" style="display:none"><br>This Christmas you are invited to a party of hard liquor, witty repartee and murder in the company of Nick and Nora Charles. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387799589i/7673286.jpg" alt="Powell &amp; Loy" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A hardboiled crime comedy might seem like an oddball choice for a winter holiday read, but Dashiell Hammett manages to mix together not only killer martinis, but also a succesful marriage between the mean and dirty Prohibition Era gumshoe detective and the British slick and sophisticated whodunits of Agatha Christie or Dorothy Sayers. Spiced up with some of that enchanting 1930's screwball comedy.<br><br>Nick Charles is a former private detective who gave up on his profession after marrying rich socialite Nora. He's now returning for the Holiday Season to New York, where he plans to play the stockmarket like a boss, enjoy the nightlife and be pleasantly drunk from the moment he wakes (after noon preferably) to the moment he goes to sleep (preferably in the early morning hours). Nora and their pet dog Asta are willing partners in the plan, their apartment door always open to old friends and former enemies of Nick and the cocktail glasses are never empty.<br><br>Pretty soon, these old friends are all pressuring Nick, some at gunpoint, to investigate the dissapearance of one of his former clients : the thin man from the title. Clyde Wynant is an elderly, cranky and eccentric inventor who managed to alienate all his relations and business partners, providing an exceedingly large list of suspects : his secretary/mistress, his former wife, his young and alluring daughter, his morbid teenage son, his ex-wife's new husband, his lawyer, a disgruntled former business asociate, his mistress' gangster boyfriend, an ex-convict that now runs a speakeasy, a police informer also interested in the secretary, and so on ... Some of them turn up dead as the investigation unfolds. Nick does his best to try to stay out of it, but Nora is thrilled by the more dangerous aspects of her husbands former lifestyle. The denouement is closer to Hercule Poirot than to Sam Spade, but very satisfying, despite the fact that I was already aware of the identity of the criminal after watching the movie several times.<br><br>The dialogue is lively and often caustic, with the easy banter between Nick and Nora nicely balancing the less savoury aspects of the suspects venal actions. The novel is actually painted in darker shades, boiled harder and more cynical than its famous movie adaptation. The exuberance of the detective couple actually serves to deepen the black shadows cast by the characters fighting over the Wynant fortune. There's a world of crooks and liars, sharks and femmes fatales outside the Nick and Nora penthouse apartment, reminding us that Hammett is rightly famous for less comedic offerings:<br><br><i> I don't like crooks. And if I did like 'em, I wouldn't like crooks that are stool pigeons. And if I did like crooks that are stool pigeons, I still wouldn't like you. </i> is just one of the memorable quotes in the novel. (I had more, but my phone decided to lose them and all my bookmarks unexpectedly)<br><br>As a conclusion, if I would be asked to choose between the two versions, I would pick the movie as my favorite : William Powell and Myrna Loy are perfect in their roles as Nick and Nora, often improvising much funnier repartees and moments of physical comedy than those found in the source material. And the dog playing Asta merits an Oscar of her own. The supporting cast is excellent, the black and white cinematography crisp and elegant - I really don't see the need for a remake, despite being a fan of Johnny Depp.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387799589i/7673287.jpg" alt="thin man gag" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The final remark of Nick at the end of the case : <i> All this excitement has put us behind in our drinking. </i><br><br>Cheers!<br>And a Merry Christmas to all Goodreaders.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16198668124397173418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1780039352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1780039352" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1780039352?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780039352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9127543311272261683">As research for a novel I'm writing, I'm reading detective fiction and ripping off everything of value. My story takes place in L.A. of the early '90s, but I'm traveling to all eras and hiring all manner of private eyes to serve as tour guide. Next up is <i>The Thin Man</i> by Dashiell Hammett. When you catch yourself in the mirror looking like Cameron Frye in <i>Ferris Bueller's Day Off</i> in a fit of paralysis by analysis, except over whether to finish a book, I think the answer there is "no." I abandoned </span>
  <span id="freeText9127543311272261683" style="display:none">As research for a novel I'm writing, I'm reading detective fiction and ripping off everything of value. My story takes place in L.A. of the early '90s, but I'm traveling to all eras and hiring all manner of private eyes to serve as tour guide. Next up is <i>The Thin Man</i> by Dashiell Hammett. When you catch yourself in the mirror looking like Cameron Frye in <i>Ferris Bueller's Day Off</i> in a fit of paralysis by analysis, except over whether to finish a book, I think the answer there is "no." I abandoned this one at the 20% mark, but will offer my reasons for not giving a one-star rating.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597374744i/29963513._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Published in December, 1933.<br><br>Nick ... and Nora Charles are a couple of dazzling urbanites celebrating the repeal of Prohibition and making up for lost time. Nick used to be a private detective. There's a murder among their social network and everyone is intent on Nick solving the crime. They have a cute Schnauzer named Asta. It's unclear whether Nora or Asta do anything more than look cute and occasionally pester the man of the house.<br><br>I haven't seen a frame of the popular film series starring William Powell and Myrna Loy, but the novel reads like a novelization of a 1930s movie. Scenes begin with someone entering a room, end when they exit and then pick up in another room, all shot on the MGM soundstages. Artifice is thick. The characters behave like characters acting in a photoplay. There's no danger that something major could occur. The story is all froth.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597377465i/29963609._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two things I'm stealing from Dashiell Hammett, however:<br><br>I liked how everywhere Nick Charles goes, people ask him if he's Nick Charles the Famous Detective. The poor chap just wants to get lit but the next thing he knows, some friend of a friend is confiding some insignificant problem they feel warrants detecting. It reminds me of how people behave when they encounter a physician, or an editor. They can't resist sharing some minor ailment bothering their mother or pitch their manuscript for <i>Bridget Jones's Diary</i> meets <i>Anna Karenina</i>. All free of charge, of course.<br><br>While Hammett is much less specific about the spirits his characters imbibe or their preparation than I expected, I was reminded how characters often do have a favorite drink and how that detail becomes part of their character. I selected a Tequila Sunrise for my detective, who attended art school on the West Coast of the 1970s. As a sufferer of social anxiety, she'd never turn down a cocktail when offered one and a Tequila Sunrise is pretty easy to make. As an artist, the aesthetic delight of how a beverage looks would be important to her. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597374382i/29963503._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So, here's to you, Mr. Hammett. Your book really wasn't for me in the year 2020, but I did become a better writer after reading one-fifth of yours.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9127543311272261683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1780039352">
  <td colspan="2">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/138935477?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/111921-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=the-movie-is-better">the-movie-is-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=the-list">the-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/111921-madeline?shelf=detective-fiction">detective-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138935477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1056249185530940914">Honestly? I think the awesomeness of Nick and Nora Charles got built up a little too much for me before I read this, because I was expecting 200 pages of nonstop witty banter between the two, and was mildly disappointed. Sure, Nick is funny in a dry sarcastic way, and Nora is the sassy drunken aunt you never knew you always wanted, but their banter and witticisms only caused the occasional chuckle. <br/><br/>But lucky for me, the book has a lot more going for it than just the banter. It's a fun, classic 3</span>
  <span id="freeText1056249185530940914" style="display:none">Honestly? I think the awesomeness of Nick and Nora Charles got built up a little too much for me before I read this, because I was expecting 200 pages of nonstop witty banter between the two, and was mildly disappointed. Sure, Nick is funny in a dry sarcastic way, and Nora is the sassy drunken aunt you never knew you always wanted, but their banter and witticisms only caused the occasional chuckle. <br /><br />But lucky for me, the book has a lot more going for it than just the banter. It's a fun, classic 30's mystery full of crazy dames and shooting and goons and coppers, and the characters drink so much it made my liver hurt just reading about it. Like <i>The Maltese Falcon</i>, it got to a point where I had to just accept that I had no idea what any of the characters were talking about and try to go with the flow until someone explained everything at the end. They mystery itself (it includes a string of murders and a suspiciously-absent man) was engrossing, although I guessed the big twist a few pages before it happened. <br /><br />Having looked up the movie version of <i>The Thin Man</i> on IMDB, I've added it to my Netflix queue and intend to make a comparison as soon as possible - if the IMDB quotes are any indication, the movie version looks much funnier than the book. Stand by for further information as soon as I watch it. <br /><br />PS: I just noticed one of the options at the bottom of the review box, next to the spoiler button - "Does this book follow a few characters or many?" Who the fuck cares, Goodreads? If I think it's that important, I'll <i>mention it in the actual review</i>. Jesus. <br /><br />UPDATE, AFTER WATCHING THE FILM VERSION: I'm now putting this on my "The Movie Is Better" shelf, because as I predicted, the movie is much funnier. William Powell and Myrna Loy are darling as Nick and Nora, Mimi is appropriately crazy (although in the movie there's never any doubt about whether she killed Julia, because we actually see her find the body), Gilbert is adorable, and Nora has an absolutely fabulous collection of outfits. Watch the movie, and read the book only if you're really curious about the little changes they made in the screenplay. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1056249185530940914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3689570923291538903" style="display:none">Captain Renault : What in heaven’s name brought you to Casablanca?<br />Rick : My health – I came to Casablanca for the waters.<br />Captain Renault : Waters? What waters? We’re in the desert.<br />Rick : I was misinformed.<br /><br />*<br /><br />Thinking Dashiell Hammett would be the go-to guy now that I have run out of Chandlers, I thought : let’s read the very famous The Thin Man. The movie is great, what could possibly go wrong?<br /><br />*<br /><br />Well, for starters, Chandler’s prose is graced with genius where Hammett’s prose is graced with deadlines. <br /><br />*<br /><br />Everyone comments on the insane amount of drinking that is detailed on every page here. Even the dog drinks manhattans. Take out all the references to hooch in The Thin Man and it would be 70 pages shorter, easy. So that was kind of silly and then irksome and then really irritating in a harrumph! kind of way. <br /><br />*<br /><br />They’ll tell you that Nick and Nora, our charming lushes, later to die of cirrhosis of the liver at the age of 55 and 46 respectively, are possessed of this witty banter. But you know, not that witty. The witty is all in the movie. <br /><br /><b>FROM THE BOOK</b><br /><br />Dorothy patted the dog’s head and left us. We found a table. Nora said : “She’s pretty.”<br /> “If you like ‘em like that.”<br /> She grinned at me : “You got types?”<br /> “Only you, darling... lanky brunettes with wicked jaws.” <br /> “And how about the redhead you wandered off with at the Quinn’s last night?”<br /> “That’s silly,” I said. “She just wanted to show me some French etchings.”<br /><br /><b>SAME SCENE FROM THE MOVIE</b><br /><br />Nora (referring to Dorothy): Pretty girl.<br /><br />Nick: If you like 'em like that.<br /><br />Nora (grinning at him) : You got types?<br /><br />Nick : Only you, darling... lanky brunettes with wicked jaws.<br /><br />Nora :	Who is she?<br /><br />Nick :	I was hoping I wouldn't have to tell you. Dorothy is really my daughter. You see, it was Spring in Venice, and I was so young. I didn't know what I was doing. We were all like that on my father's side.<br /><br />Nora : By the way, how is your father's side?<br /><br />Nick : Much better, thanks.<br /><br />Nora : How many drinks have you had?<br /><br />Nick : Six Martinis.<br /><br />Nora (to the waiter, ordering) : Six Martinis. (then to Nick)You're not going to have anything on me.<br /><br />*<br /><br />Then there was the plot. I couldn’t muster up the energy to wonder who clobbered Dr Plum in the library with the blunt instrument.<br /><br />*<br /><br />So in answer to the question what could possibly go wrong, sort of everything did all at once.</span>

<div id="review_1097830987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097830987" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097830987?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=detective-books">detective-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=noir">noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097830987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10369459013802236889">Nick and Nora Charles are staying at a swanky hotel in Manhattan when word arrives of a missing man. Content to leave his old life behind as a private detective, Nick wants no part of the investigation. However, it isn’t long before Nick is forced into the case and in order to deal with the cast of characters circling the search, he keeps the liquor flowing.<br/><br/>Ah, the 1930s, when alcoholism was considered a charming personality trait as well as the social norm rather than the life-destroying diseas</span>
  <span id="freeText10369459013802236889" style="display:none">Nick and Nora Charles are staying at a swanky hotel in Manhattan when word arrives of a missing man. Content to leave his old life behind as a private detective, Nick wants no part of the investigation. However, it isn’t long before Nick is forced into the case and in order to deal with the cast of characters circling the search, he keeps the liquor flowing.<br /><br />Ah, the 1930s, when alcoholism was considered a charming personality trait as well as the social norm rather than the life-destroying disease that it is today. Seriously, I have no idea how Nick Charles was even standing at points let alone aware enough to piece together clues and solve a murder mystery.<br /><br />It goes without saying how tremendous a character his wife Nora is as the author makes her just as important a character as Nick. She exists in an era that I do not imagine had many strong female protagonists. Outside of the two main attractions, the cast is filled with characters with their personalities turned up to eleven. Don’t get me started on the always hysterical Dorothy.<br /><br />While I didn’t like this as much as Hammett’s classic Sam Spade novel The Maltese Falcon, it was still a fun, whodunnit featuring hilariously witty dialogue along with two memorable leads. While Hammett is considered the Godfather to all hard-boiled fiction, Chandler certainly perfected it with his Philip Marlowe series.<br /><br />Also posted @ <a href="http://everyreadthing.com/2014/11/27/the-thin-man/" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Read Thing</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10369459013802236889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
